Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Piatt 11-17H
Figure 1. Ensign #161 at the Marathon Oil Company Piatt 11-17H location, as the sun goes down in September
of 2014 (Kate Schwehr, Well-site Geologist, Sunburst Consulting, Inc.)
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company Piatt 11-17H well is located approximately 7 miles northwest of
Manning in Dunn County, North Dakota [NW NW Section 17, T144N, R96W]. The Piatt 11-
17H is a single, double section, horizontal Bakken well that's part of a multi-well pad to be
drilled by Marathon's newly acquired rig, Ensign 161 (Figure 1). The targeted, Middle Bakken
Member is known as a mixed carbonate-clastic sequence stratigraphically sequenced between
two petroliferous, carbonaceous black shales, the Upper Bakken Shale and the Lower Bakken
Shale. The two shales combined serve as the prospect source rock.
PLAN
The drilling plan stipulated that the vertical hole inclination be held at an inclination of 3.00º
with an azimuth of 295° from surface casing, at 2,340', until approximately 10,263' MD where
the curve would be kicked-off for a 12º per 100' curve until landing, at approximately 11,455'
MD (10,837' TVD) in the Middle Bakken. The landing target was set 15' below the top of the
upper shale member. After landing, intermediate casing would then be set and cemented to
isolate the target reservoir, and the lateral would commence. The lateral would continue south at
roughly 180º to a bottom hole location within SE SE of Section 19, T144N-R96W.
OFFSET CONTROL
Top and thickness control was provided by three main offsets (Figure 2). The following offset
wells provided gamma signatures to correlate formation tops; allowing thickness evaluation for a
proper target landing. The three offsets include:
The MOC Louie Hendricks 24-20H which is located approximately 2 miles south of
the subject well and is a horizontal middle Bakken well, drilled in June of 2009. The
horizontal path parallels the projected path of the Piatt 11-17H, so this offset will be
used to compare structure and gamma character.
The Davis Oil Co. Murphy Creek State 1 which is located approximately 1.3 miles
east of the Piatt 11-17H. The Murphy Creek State 1 is a vertical hole, drilled in
December of 1983 into the Duperow Formation, and is classified as a dry hole. This
offset is used to land the well and see the entire middle Bakken gamma signature.
The MOC Hecker 21-5H which is located approximately 2 miles north of the subject
well. It was drilled in July of 2007, horizontally through the middle Bakken and will
be useful to compare gamma signature.
The subject well was the first vertical-curve segment drilled on the five well pad. One of these
five wells (Kary 11-17H) drilled south, paralleling the subject well, so it was also used for
structure control during the lateral section (Figure 3).
Figure 2. Map showing the location of the Marathon Oil Company Piatt 11-17H and the
location of the three wells used for offset control (NDIC, ArcMap GIS, 2014)
ENGINEERING
The well spud on September 14, 2014 with Ensign 161. The surface hole was drilled to 2,340'
MD with freshwater. Here, 9 5/8" casing was run to 2,328' MD, isolating the surface hole. The
remaining vertical hole was drilled with diesel invert drilling fluid, with a target weight of 8.8 to
9.8 pounds/gallon. The vertical was completed with three assemblies, after reaching a kick-off
point of 10,170' MD. Here, electric logs were run before starting the curve build section. The
curve was drilled utilizing a 2.38° mud motor and completed at 11,280' MD (10,883' TVD),
after 19 hours. Intermediate 7" surface casing was set and cemented to 11,251' MD, before the
rig continued batch drilling four other vertical, curve and lateral sections.
The rig returned to the subject location on December 8, 2014. The lateral commenced using a
saltwater based drilling fluid, and drilled to total depth on December 16, 2014. Four assembly
combinations, using two separate PDC bits ahead of BHI 5" XLP motors, drilled the lateral
section. The Piatt 11-17H reached a total depth of 21,051' at 14:30 MT on December 16th, 2014.
The bottom hole location is 9,990.33' south and 970.50' west of surface location or 210.14' FSL
& 3.80' FEL, SE SE Section 19, T144N, R96W (Figure 3).

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Onsite-geologic supervision was provided by Sunburst Consulting, Inc. for the Piatt 11-17H.
The geology wellsite team monitored gas, logged drill cuttings, and picked formation tops.
Logging samples and gas monitoring started at 8,650' MD. The rig crew caught drill cuttings in
30' lagged intervals. Drill cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope and complete
lithological descriptions are provided in the appendix of this report. Dried sample cuttings were
sent to the Marathon address, as well as to the NDIC. A Pason digital gas detector was interfaced
with Epoch, an electronic data recorder (EDR). The Epoch system provided hole depth, bit
depth and pump rates to the gas detector and distributed the detector's total gas readings across
location.
Total gas was recorded in units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air), and
chromatography of C1 ­ C4 components were calculated in parts-per-million.
Electric logs were run from surface casing (2,328' MD) to 10,170'MD. Weatherford provided
the service. The triple combo was run, which includes neutron/density, gamma, and array
induction. The E-logs provided further evaluation of possible zones of interest that were noted
during drilling with the initial MWD gamma data, gas shows, and sample evaluations.
Calculations from the E-log data were performed on the selected intervals of possible interest to
determine hydrocarbon and porosity levels. A chart with the calculations is included in an
appendix to this well evaluation. No prospective intervals of interest were determined after
performing water saturation calculations.
Lithology
Beginning in the Mississippian Kibbey Formation, sample logging continued through the
Mississippian-Devonian, Middle Bakken Member. The Bakken Formation is the only lithology
discussed in detail, complete sample descriptions by depth can be found in an addendum to this
report.
The Bakken Formation, Upper Bakken Shale Member was penetrated at 10,857' TVD (-8,736'
MSL). This member is easily recognized by a sharp increase and sustained high gamma ray
counts, a marked increase in penetration rates, and typically sustained higher gas shows. The
upper member is a distinct black, petroliferous & carbonaceous shale containing occasional to
common disseminated and nodular pyrite (Figure 4). The Middle Bakken Member was
penetrated at 10,872' TVD (-8,451' MSL). The middle member consists of a siltstone (Figure
4), limestone and silty sandstone. The target zone consists of light to medium gray-brown silty
sandstone, containing fine intergranular porosity and light spotty to even brown oil staining.
Landing & Geosteering
The prognosis called for a landing target 14' into the Middle Bakken Member, at a depth of
10,837' TVD. Using gamma signatures from offset wells, well-site geologists were able to
correlate formation tops in order to make any necessary corrections to the prognosis landing
target. Tops and markers came in ~30' low to prognosis. The difference increased closer to
landing, with the Lodgepole coming in 55' low to the original prognosis. The target was moved
down, to 10,872' TVD, after picking the Lodgepole top and then were revised as the Lodgepole
markers came in, dropping again to 10,880' TVD. When the False Bakken was intersected, the
target was re-adjusted to 10,887' TVD. The well landed at approximately 10,883' TVD, 11'
TVD below the top of the Middle Bakken Member.
Three primary gamma signatures were used to steer the well in an 8' thick geologic window.
Throughout our target interval, gamma counts ranged from roughly 35-80 (API), and oscillated
with regularity. This gamma trend was pervasive throughout our entire zone, which proposed a
challenge in determining our precise location in target, within the laminated facies. Two other
primary markers were observed above and below our target zone. Above the zone, a reliable
packestone layer with 20-30 (API) gamma counts was observed. Within the packstone, counts
upwards of 115 (API) were also observed, indicating possible laminar limestone deposition. At
the bottom of our target interval, a hotter and tighter gamma marker was observed with (API)
counts of 70-85. This marker bounded our target zone below and was encountered several times
during the lateral. These markers provided data upon which formation dip was calculated, and
were consistent throughout the lateral.
The target window in the Middle Bakken was entered at approximately 11,170' MD, and the
well-bore was maintained in the target for approximately 80% of the lateral. Over the course of
the 9,886' exposure to the middle member, structure gained a total of 41.00' TVD, resulting in a
gross apparent dip of +0.24° (Figure 5).

Hydrocarbons
A slight increase in gas values were observed towards the bottom of the Mission Canyon within
the Fryburg interval. Gas shows, between 80 & 100 units were observed in this interval,
eventually increasing again towards the base of the Lodgepole Formation to over 100 units.
While drilling the curve through the lower Lodgepole, False Bakken, and Upper Bakken Shale
Member, gas increased to over 5,000 units. These shows can most likely be attributed to high
hydrocarbon content in the Upper Bakken Shale, as well as zones of possible fracture porosity
towards the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation.
Background gas throughout the lateral ranged from 300 - 2,000 units, with an average of around
1,100 units. Several intervals of the lateral produced notable increases in background gas and gas
shows. The highest gas shows were observed while the well drilled towards the bottom of our
target window, however apart from this observation, there is little evidence to link high gas
shows to a particular portion of our drilling window. Observed increases are likely a result of
localized zones of high porosity, overpressure and possible fracture porosity.
Light brown oil was observed coming over the shakers throughout the lateral. Spotty to even
brown oil staining was observed in sample for the entire duration of the lateral, and fluorescent
cuts of samples yielded primarily moderate to fast streaming green-blue cuts.
Gas was vented through the gas buster beginning at 12,675' MD, and circulated through the gas
buster beginning at 12,706' MD and continuing throughout the remainder of the lateral. 20-40'
trip flares were observed while tripping in the hole at 12,675' and 12,706' MD. After
commencing the lateral after 12,706' MD, a 5-10' intermittent flare was observed for the
remainder of the well. No back-pressure was held during the well (Figure 6).

SUMMARY
The Marathon Oil Company, Piatt 11-17H was drilled in approximately 20 days, reaching a total
depth of 21,051' MD on December 16th, 2014. The lateral portion of the well exposed 9,886' of
the Middle Bakken Member, and was determined to be 80% within the target interval. Samples
from the Middle Bakken consisted of light to medium gray-brown silty sandstone with fine
intergranular porosity and light, spotty brown oil staining.
An overall dip of +0.24° was
calculated using a combination of gamma ray, sample analysis, and drilling parameter data.
Despite the challenges presented by the lack of reliable gamma markers directly within our target
interval and relatively thin Middle Bakken interval, the well proved to be an engineering and
geologic success. Sample analyses combined with gas data provide strong evidence that the Piatt
11-17H will be a successful Middle Bakken well. The project currently awaits fracture
stimulation to maximize its full potential as an oil and gas well.
Respectfully submitted,
Kate Schwehr
Nathan Stansfield
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
December 16th, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Marathon Oil Company ­ Piatt 11-17H
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A detailed list of
sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma ray marker tops have been
inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular
microscope. The drilling fluid was diesel based invert from surface casing to 11,280' and changed to salt-water
from 11,280' to 21,051' (TD). Sample collection began at 8,650'.
Kibbey Formation
8650-8680 SILTSTONE: red to brown, occasional red to orange, firm to friable, crystalline, sub-blocky to blocky,
calcite cemented, poorly cemented
8680-8710 SILTSTONE: red to brown, occasional red to orange, firm to friable, crystalline, sub-blocky to blocky,
calcite cemented, poorly cemented; trace ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline, soft, amorphous
8710-8740 ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline, soft, amorphous; rare to occasional SILTSTONE:
red, occasional red to brown, soft to friable, crystalline, sub-blocky to blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented

HORIZONTAL WELL
PIATT 11-17H
NWNW Section 17-144N-96W
Dunn County
Well File # 29246
Dear Natalie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24151, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is granted on
the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement shall be located approximately down the north-south axis (500'
drilling corridor, per Commission policy) and no closer than 200 feet to the north or south boundary within the 2560 acre spacing unit
consisting of Sections 17, 18, 19 & 20 T144N R96W. Tool error need not be considered except when deemed necessary by the
Director pursuant to order.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must be
maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-
back whenever filtration operations are conducted. All distances on the Production Layout Plat must comply with NDAC 43-
02-03-28 (SAFETY REGULATION). MARATHON OIL COMPANY must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety
Regulation) when contemplating simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28
(Safety Regulation) "No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any
producing well or oil tank." MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to
location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and completion
operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of the land surface and
freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized
representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director
prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The proposed directional
plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is: 701'W. Also, based on the azimuth of the
proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10000'S and 1201'W.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved drilling permit
on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd business day following
publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn
affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and
any other information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit,
the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given immediately upon the
spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information
must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding.
Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Natalie Menge
August 26, 2014
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a certified
copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or
in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the
survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one
adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when sliding) and 90
feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby granted. Such
information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records wherever located.
Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the Director and his representatives to come
upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and
operation of such wells and to have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The
information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission and
its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail cement
utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and porosity zones
can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and (3) a log from which the
presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation log) in every well in which production
or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as
one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a
standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture

Gas Capture Plan
Kary Pad
Sec 17 T144N R96W
Field: Murphy Creek
Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
The wellpad is expected to commence production around May 2015. It is anticipated that this well will be
connected at first production.
Multi-well startup
The wells are expected to flowback concurrently with one of the other wells on the location. Flowback of each well
is expected to be approximately 4-10 days in duration.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 800 MSCFD
Average Oil Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 1,900 bopd

Alternatives to flaring

location as well as connection to a gas pipeline.
Other alternatives to flaring are noted in NDIC order 24665
